CC   -!- FUNCTION: Calcium-binding protein that modulates excitation-
CC       contraction coupling in the heart. Contributes to calcium
CC       homeostasis in the heart sarcoplasmic reticulum. Modulates the
CC       activity of RYR2 calcium channels. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12824171}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homodimer. Interacts with GCA, RYR2 and ANXA7 (By
CC       similarity). {ECO:0000250}.

CC       Sarcoplasmic reticulum membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12824171};
CC       Peripheral membrane protein {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12824171};
CC       Cytoplasmic side {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12824171}. Note=Relocates to
CC       the sarcoplasmic reticulum membrane in response to elevated
CC       calcium levels.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Extremely potent competitive inhibitor of cAMP-dependent
CC       protein kinase activity, this protein interacts with the catalytic
CC       subunit of the enzyme after the cAMP-induced dissociation of its
CC       regulatory chains.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Highest expression in muscle (both skeletal
CC       and cardiac) and brain.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: The inhibitory site contains regions very similar
CC       to the hinge regions (sites that directly interact with the enzyme
CC       active site) and "pseudosubstrate site" of the regulatory chains;
CC       but, unlike these chains, PKI does not contain cAMP-binding sites.
CC       The arginine residues within the inhibitory site are essential for
CC       inhibition and recognition of the enzyme active site (By
CC       similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the PKI family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Adapter protein that interacts with EDAR DEATH domain
CC       and couples the receptor to EDA signaling pathway during
CC       morphogenesis of ectodermal organs. Mediates the activation of NF-
CC       kappa-B. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11882293}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Self-associates and binds EDAR, TRAF1, TRAF2 and TRAF3.

CC   -!- DISEASE: Ectodermal dysplasia 11A, hypohidrotic/hair/nail type,
CC       autosomal dominant (ECTD11A) [MIM:614940]: A form of ectodermal
CC       dysplasia, a heterogeneous group of disorders due to abnormal
CC       development of two or more ectodermal structures. It is an
CC       autosomal dominant condition characterized by hypotrichosis,
CC       abnormal or missing teeth, and hypohidrosis due to the absence of
CC       sweat glands. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17354266,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20979233}. Note=The disease is caused by
CC       mutations affecting the gene represented in this entry.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Ectodermal dysplasia 11B, hypohidrotic/hair/tooth type,
CC       autosomal recessive (ECTD11B) [MIM:614941]: A disorder due to
CC       abnormal development of two or more ectodermal structures, and
CC       characterized by sparse hair (atrichosis or hypotrichosis),
CC       abnormal or missing teeth and the inability to sweat due to the
CC       absence of sweat glands. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11780064,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:17354266, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20222921}.
CC       Note=The disease is caused by mutations affecting the gene
CC       represented in this entry.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: The coatomer is a cytosolic protein complex that binds
CC       to dilysine motifs and reversibly associates with Golgi non-
CC       clathrin-coated vesicles, which further mediate biosynthetic
CC       protein transport from the ER, via the Golgi up to the trans Golgi
CC       network. Coatomer complex is required for budding from Golgi
CC       membranes, and is essential for the retrograde Golgi-to-ER
CC       transport of dilysine-tagged proteins. In mammals, the coatomer
CC       can only be recruited by membranes associated to ADP-ribosylation
CC       factors (ARFs), which are small GTP-binding proteins; the complex
CC       also influences the Golgi structural integrity, as well as the
CC       processing, activity, and endocytic recycling of LDL receptors.
CC       Involved in the Golgi disassembly and reassembly processes during
CC       cell cycle. Involved in autophagy by playing a role in early
CC       endosome function. Plays a role in organellar compartmentalization
CC       of secretory compartments including endoplasmic reticulum (ER)-
CC       Golgi intermediate compartment (ERGIC), Golgi, trans-Golgi network
CC       (TGN) and recycling endosomes, and in biosynthetic transport of
CC       CAV1. Plays a functional role in facilitating the transport of
CC       kappa-type opioid receptor mRNAs into axons and enhances
CC       translation of these proteins in the axonal compartment of dorsal
CC       root ganglion (DRG) cells. Required for limiting lipid storage in
CC       lipid droplets. Involved in lipid homeostasis by regulating the
CC       presence of perilipin family members PLIN2 and PLIN3 at the lipid
CC       droplet surface and promoting the association of adipocyte
CC       triglyceride lipase (PNPLA2) with the lipid droplet surface to
CC       mediate lipolysis. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17698811,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:1957170, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20056612,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8376457}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Oligomeric complex that consists of at least the alpha,
CC       beta, beta', gamma, delta, epsilon and zeta subunits. Interacts
CC       with SCYL1. Interacts with CAPN8 (By similarity). Interacts with
CC       COPG1 (By similarity). Interacts with ARF1 (myristoylated); this
CC       interaction is required for binding of COPB1 to Golgi membranes
CC       (By similarity). Interacts (via trunk domain) with ARF1 (via
CC       switch I region); the interaction is direct (By similarity).
CC       Interacts with KCNK2 (via N-terminus); this interaction increases
CC       the channel-mediated whole cell currents and promotes plasma
CC       membrane expression of KCNK2 (By similarity). Interacts with
CC       PRKCE. Interacts with STX17. Interacts with TMEM115 (By
CC       similarity). {ECO:0000250, ECO:0000269|PubMed:18556652,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:21545355, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8376457,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:9360998}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P53619:ARCN1 (xeno); NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-620488, EBI-620432;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cytoplasm {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8376457,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8458872}. Golgi apparatus membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10359600, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10402461,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:12486083, ECO:0000269|PubMed:1957170,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20056612, ECO:0000269|PubMed:8376457,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8458872}; Peripheral membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P53618}; Cytoplasmic side {ECO:0000305}.
CC       Cytoplasmic vesicle, COPI-coated vesicle membrane
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:10359600, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15749703,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8458872}; Peripheral membrane protein;
CC       Cytoplasmic side {ECO:0000305}. Cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P53618}. Endoplasmic reticulum-Golgi
CC       intermediate compartment {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q9JIF7}. Microsome
CC       membrane {ECO:0000269|PubMed:9165027}. Note=The coatomer is
CC       cytoplasmic or polymerized on the cytoplasmic side of the Golgi,
CC       as well as on the vesicles/buds originating from it
CC       (PubMed:8458872). Proteolytic cleavage by CAPN8 triggers
CC       translocation from Golgi to cytoplasm (By similarity). Found in
CC       perinuclear vesicular-tubular clusters (VTCs) and in the Golgi
CC       region where associated with vesicles, buds and rims of the Golgi
CC       stack (PubMed:8458872). Occasionally present at the trans-side of
CC       Golgi, but mainly present at the cis-Golgi side in transitional
CC       areas (TA), on so-called peripheral elements (PE) consisting of
CC       tubules and vesicles located between the cup-shaped transitional
CC       elements (TE) of the rough endoplasmic reticulum (RER) and the
CC       cis-most Golgi cisternae (PubMed:8458872). Present in cytoplasm,
CC       not associated with visible coats or membranes, with a minor
CC       fraction present on small clusters of tubules and vesicles
CC       (PubMed:8458872). Some association with high-density and low-
CC       density microsomes and mitochondria/nuclei fraction
CC       (PubMed:9165027). Very little found in plasma membrane fraction
CC       (PubMed:9165027). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q9JIF7,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:8458872, ECO:0000269|PubMed:9165027}.
CC   -!- PTM: Proteolytically cleaved between Ser-528 and Ser-529 by CAPN8.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- MISCELLANEOUS: Brefeldin A induces dissociation from the Golgi of
CC       the beta-COP and presumably the other coatomer subunits.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Functions as a RHOA-specific guanine nucleotide exchange
CC       factor regulating signaling pathways downstream of integrins and
CC       growth factor receptors. Functions in axonal branching, synapse
CC       formation and dendritic morphogenesis. Functions also in focal
CC       adhesion formation, cell motility and B-lymphocytes activation.
CC       May regulate NEFL expression and aggregation and play a role in
CC       apoptosis (By similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homooligomer; forms cytoplasmic aggregates. Forms a
CC       complex with MAPK8 and MAPK8IP1. Interacts with RHOA. Interacts
CC       with microtubules. Interacts with YWHAE and YWHAH. Interacts with
CC       PTK2/FAK1. Interacts with NEFL (By similarity). Interacts with
CC       CTNND2; prevents interaction with RHOA. {ECO:0000250,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:10574993, ECO:0000269|PubMed:17993462}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cytoplasm {ECO:0000250}. Cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250}. Note=Colocalizes with the microtubule radial and
CC       cortical systems. {ECO:0000250}.

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [MRNA].
RC   STRAIN=Wistar; TISSUE=Placenta;
RX   PubMed=12493714; DOI=10.1095/biolreprod.102.008565;
RA   Arai K.Y., Tsuchida K., Uehara K., Taya K., Sugino H.;
RT   "Characterization of rat follistatin-related gene: effects of estrous
RT   cycle stage and pregnancy on its messenger RNA expression in rat
RT   reproductive tissues.";
RL   Biol. Reprod. 68:199-206(2003).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: The secreted form is a binding and antagonizing protein
CC       for members of the TGF-beta family, such us activin, BMP2 and
CC       MSTN. Inhibits activin A-, activin B-, BMP2- and MSDT-induced
CC       cellular signaling; more effective on activin A than on activin B.
CC       Involved in bone formation; inhibits osteoclast differentiation.
CC       Involved in hematopoiesis; involved in differentiation of
CC       hemopoietic progenitor cells, increases hematopoietic cell
CC       adhesion to fibronectin and seems to contribute to the adhesion of
CC       hematopoietic precursor cells to the bone marrow stroma. The
CC       nuclear form is probably involved in transcriptional regulation
CC       via interaction with MLLT10 (By similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with INHBA and INHBB. Interacts with FN1.
CC       Interacts with ADAM12. Interacts with MLLT10; the interaction
CC       enhances MLLT10 in vitro transcriptional activity and self-
CC       association. Interacts with MSTN (By similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted {ECO:0000250}. Nucleus
CC       {ECO:0000250}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Pore-forming (alpha) subunit of voltage-gated potassium
CC       channel. Elicits an outward current, but shows no inactivation.
CC       Channel properties may be modulated by cAMP and subunit assembly.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: The potassium channel is probably composed of a homo- or
CC       heterotetrameric complex of pore-forming alpha subunits that can
CC       associate with modulating beta subunits.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Highly expressed in adult testis, and in adult
CC       and embryonic brain. In adult brain found in piriform cortex,
CC       olfactory tubercle, cerebral cortex, hippocampus pyramidial cells
CC       and dentate gyrus and basal ganglia of caudate/putamen and
CC       accumbens nucleus. Detected at intermediate levels in lung, spinal
CC       cord, and pituitary. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11425889,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:9824707}.
CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: Expressed at day E18 in embryonic brain.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The segment S4 is probably the voltage-sensor and is
CC       characterized by a series of positively charged amino acids at
CC       every third position.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the potassium channel family. H (Eag) (TC
CC       1.A.1.20) subfamily. Kv12.3/KCNH4 sub-subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.

RP   NUCLEOTIDE SEQUENCE [LARGE SCALE MRNA].
RC   TISSUE=Brain;
RX   PubMed=15489334; DOI=10.1101/gr.2596504;
RG   The MGC Project Team;
RT   "The status, quality, and expansion of the NIH full-length cDNA
RT   project: the Mammalian Gene Collection (MGC).";
RL   Genome Res. 14:2121-2127(2004).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the initial reaction in O-linked
CC       oligosaccharide biosynthesis, the transfer of an N-acetyl-D-
CC       galactosamine residue to a serine or threonine residue on the
CC       protein receptor. Although it displays a much weaker activity
CC       toward all substrates tested compared to GALNT2, it is able to
CC       transfer up to seven GalNAc residues to the Muc5AC peptide,
CC       suggesting that it can fill vicinal Thr/Ser residues in
CC       cooperation with other GALNT proteins. Prefers Muc1a as substrate.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: UDP-N-acetyl-alpha-D-galactosamine +
CC       polypeptide = UDP + N-acetyl-alpha-D-galactosaminyl-polypeptide.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15147861}.
CC   -!- COFACTOR:
CC       Name=Mn(2+); Xref=ChEBI:CHEBI:29035; Evidence={ECO:0000250};
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Protein modification; protein glycosylation.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Golgi apparatus membrane {ECO:0000250};
CC       Single-pass type II membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Widely expressed. Highly expressed in small
CC       intestine, placenta, spleen, cerebral cortex and ovary. Expressed
CC       at intermediate level in uterus, mammary gland, stomach,
CC       cerebellum and whole brain. Weakly expressed in fetal brain, bone
CC       marrow, thyroid gland, thymus, heart, skeletal muscle, lung,
CC       liver, colon, pancreas, kidney and testis. Not expressed in
CC       leukocyte. Expressed in both normal and osteoarthritic cartilage.
CC       Expressed at low level in chondrocytes in all zones of both normal
CC       and osteoarthritic cartilage. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11597177,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15147861}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: There are two conserved domains in the glycosyltransferase
CC       region: the N-terminal domain (domain A, also called GT1 motif),
CC       which is probably involved in manganese coordination and substrate
CC       binding and the C-terminal domain (domain B, also called
CC       Gal/GalNAc-T motif), which is probably involved in catalytic
CC       reaction and UDP-Gal binding. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The ricin B-type lectin domain binds to GalNAc and
CC       contributes to the glycopeptide specificity. {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the glycosyltransferase 2 family. GalNAc-T
CC       subfamily. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- CAUTION: Was originally termed Galnt15/pp-GaNTase 15.
CC       {ECO:0000305|PubMed:15147861}.

CC       Sequence=CAD89983.1; Type=Frameshift; Positions=169, 192, 206, 222, 270; Evidence={ECO:0000305};

CC   -!- DEVELOPMENTAL STAGE: First detected at E9.25, specifically in the
CC       mesonephric vesicles. By E10.0 expression is also observed in the
CC       rostro-lateral mandibular mesenchyme immediately adjacent to the
CC       maxillary processes. In the developing limb buds it is expressed
CC       in a unique mesenchymal domain and the onset of the expression
CC       follows a distinct dorsal to ventral developmental time sequence
CC       beginning in the forelimb and then in the hindlimb. It exhibits a
CC       dynamic expression pattern during craniofacial development, in the
CC       mandibular and maxillary processes as well as the developing
CC       palate. It is also expressed at sites of epithelial-mesenchymal
CC       interactions during tooth and kidney development.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11520675}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the Odd C2H2-type zinc-finger protein
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Facilitative glucose transporter. This isoform likely
CC       mediates the bidirectional transfer of glucose across the plasma
CC       membrane of hepatocytes and is responsible for uptake of glucose
CC       by the beta cells; may comprise part of the glucose-sensing
CC       mechanism of the beta cell. May also participate with the
CC       Na(+)/glucose cotransporter in the transcellular transport of
CC       glucose in the small intestine and kidney.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Membrane; Multi-pass membrane protein.
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: In embryo, expressed in endoderm layer of yolk
CC       sac and liver primordium. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:1289053}.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated; required for stability and retention at the
CC       cell surface of pancreatic beta cells.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:16377570}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the major facilitator superfamily. Sugar
CC       transporter (TC 2.A.1.1) family. Glucose transporter subfamily.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC       inactive.
CC   -!- PTM: There are 9 conserved cysteine residues in sensory guanylate

CC       intra- or interchain disulfide bonds.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Motor for anterograde transport of mitochondria. Has a
CC       microtubule plus end-directed motility (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Isoform 1 mediates the transport of synaptic vesicles in
CC       neuronal cells. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12204119}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Interacts with KBP (By similarity). Interacts (via C-
CC       terminus end of the kinesin-motor domain) with CHP1; the
CC       interaction occurs in a calcium-dependent manner. {ECO:0000250,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:12204119}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       P61023:Chp1; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-6143515, EBI-917838;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cytoplasmic vesicle
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:12204119}. Cytoplasm, cytoskeleton
CC       {ECO:0000250}. Mitochondrion {ECO:0000250}. Note=Colocalizes with
CC       synaptophysin at synaptic cytoplasmic transport vesicles in the
CC       neurites of hippocampal neurons. Isoform 2 is involved in the
CC       translocation of lysosomes from perinuclear regions to the cell
CC       periphery.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Rab effector involved in exocytosis. May act as scaffold
CC       protein. Plays a role in dendrite formation by melanocytes (By
CC       similarity). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q9UQ26}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Heterodimer with PCLO. Part of a ternary complex
CC       involving PCLO and EPAC2. Interacts with RAB3C, RAB3D and RAB26
CC       (By similarity). Binds RAB3A and RAB3B that have been activated by
CC       GTP-binding. Interacts with TSPOAP1 and RIMBP2. Interacts with
CC       PPFIA3 and PPFIA4. Interacts via its zinc finger with the first C2
CC       domain of UNC13A. Forms a complex consisting of UNC13A, RIMS2 and
CC       RAB3A. {ECO:0000250, ECO:0000269|PubMed:10748113,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:11797009, ECO:0000269|PubMed:16052212,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:16732694}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q62768:Unc13a; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-6972631, EBI-15584670;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Cell membrane {ECO:0000250}; Peripheral
CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000250}. Cell junction, synapse
CC       {ECO:0000250}. Cell junction, synapse, presynaptic cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250}; Peripheral membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Can convert androstan-3-alpha,17-beta-diol (3-alpha-
CC       diol) to androsterone in vitro, suggesting that it may participate
CC       in androgen metabolism during steroidogenesis. May act by
CC       metabolizing compounds that stimulate steroid synthesis and/or by
CC       generating metabolites that inhibit it. Has no activity toward
CC       DHEA (dehydroepiandrosterone), or A-dione (4-androste-3,17-dione),
CC       and only a slight activity toward testosterone to A-dione.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: 17-beta-estradiol + NAD(P)(+) = estrone +
CC       NAD(P)H. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:11165019}.

CC       relevance of such result remains unclear.

CC       Event=Alternative splicing; Named isoforms=2;

CC   -!- DOMAIN: The spacer domain and the TSP type-1 domains are important
CC       for a tight interaction with the extracellular matrix.
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- DOMAIN: The conserved cysteine present in the cysteine-switch
CC       motif binds the catalytic zinc ion, thus inhibiting the enzyme.
CC       The dissociation of the cysteine from the zinc ion upon the
CC       activation-peptide release activates the enzyme (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- PTM: May be cleaved by a furin endopeptidase (By similarity). The
CC       precursor is sequentially processed. {ECO:0000250,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15192113}.
CC   -!- PTM: N-glycosylated. Can be O-fucosylated by POFUT2 on a serine or
CC       a threonine residue found within the consensus sequence C1-X(2)-
CC       (S/T)-C2-G of the TSP type-1 repeat domains where C1 and C2 are
CC       the first and second cysteine residue of the repeat, respectively.
CC       Fucosylated repeats can then be further glycosylated by the
CC       addition of a beta-1,3-glucose residue by the glucosyltransferase,
CC       B3GALTL. Fucosylation mediates the efficient secretion of ADAMTS
CC       family members. Also can be C-glycosylated with one or two mannose
CC       molecules on tryptophan residues within the consensus sequence W-
CC       X-X-W of the TPRs. N- and C-glycosylations can also facilitate
CC       secretion (By similarity). O-glycosylated proteoglycan. Contains
CC       chondroitin sulfate. {ECO:0000250, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15192113}.

RX   PubMed=15489334; DOI=10.1101/gr.2596504;

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Required for optimal lysosomal function. Blocks EGF-
CC       stimulated EGFR intraluminal sorting and degradation. Conversely
CC       by binding with the phosphatidylinositol 4,5-bisphosphate,
CC       regulates its PIP5K1C interaction, inhibits HGS ubiquitination and
CC       relieves LAPTM4B inhibition of EGFR degradation. Recruits SLC3A2
CC       and SLC7A5 (the Leu transporter) to the lysosome, promoting entry
CC       of leucine and other essential amino acid (EAA) into the lysosome,
CC       stimulating activation of proton-transporting vacuolar (V)-ATPase
CC       protein pump (V-ATPase) and hence mTORC1 activation. Plays a role
CC       as negative regulator of TGFB1 production in regulatory T cells.
CC       Binds ceramide and facilitates its exit from late endosome in
CC       order to control cell death pathways.
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Homooligomer; upon reaching the lysosomes. Interacts with
CC       MCOLN1. Interacts with NEDD4; may play a role in the lysosomal
CC       sorting of LAPTM4B; enhances HGS association with NEDD4; mediates
CC       inhibition of EGFR degradation. Interacts with PIP5K1C; promotes
CC       SNX5 association with LAPTM4B; kinase activity of PIP5K1C is
CC       required; interaction is regulated by phosphatidylinositol 4,5-
CC       bisphosphate generated by PIP5K1C. Interacts with HGS; promotes
CC       HGS ubiquitination. Interacts with SNX5. Interacts with SLC3A2 AND
CC       SLC7A5; recruits SLC3A2 and SLC7A5 to lysosomes to promote leucine
CC       uptake into these organelles and is required for mTORC1
CC       activation. Interacts with LRRC32; decreases TGFB1 production in
CC       regulatory T cells. Interacts with BECN1; competes with EGFR for
CC       LAPTM4B binding; regulates EGFR activity. Interacts with EGFR;
CC       positively correlates with EGFR activation.
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Endomembrane system
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}; Multi-pass membrane protein
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}. Late endosome membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}. Cell membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}. Cell projection
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}. Lysosome membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}. Endosome membrane
CC       {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}. Endosome, multivesicular body
CC       membrane {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}. Endosome, multivesicular
CC       body lumen {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}.
CC   -!- PTM: Undergoes proteolytic cleavage following delivery to the
CC       lysosomes. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}.
CC   -!- PTM: Ubiquitinated by NEDD4. {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q86VI4}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the LAPTM4/LAPTM5 transporter family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Component of the PAF1 complex (PAF1C) which has multiple
CC       functions during transcription by RNA polymerase II and is
CC       implicated in regulation of development and maintenance of
CC       embryonic stem cell pluripotency. PAF1C associates with RNA
CC       polymerase II through interaction with POLR2A CTD non-
CC       phosphorylated and 'Ser-2'- and 'Ser-5'-phosphorylated forms and
CC       is involved in transcriptional elongation, acting both
CC       indepentently and synergistically with TCEA1 and in cooperation
CC       with the DSIF complex and HTATSF1. PAF1C is required for
CC       transcription of Hox and Wnt target genes. PAF1C is involved in
CC       hematopoiesis and stimulates transcriptional activity of
CC       KMT2A/MLL1; it promotes leukemogenesis through association with
CC       KMT2A/MLL1-rearranged oncoproteins, such as KMT2A/MLL1-MLLT3/AF9
CC       and KMT2A/MLL1-MLLT1/ENL. PAF1C is involved in histone
CC       modifications such as ubiquitination of histone H2B and
CC       methylation on histone H3 'Lys-4' (H3K4me3). PAF1C recruits the
CC       RNF20/40 E3 ubiquitin-protein ligase complex and the E2 enzyme
CC       UBE2A or UBE2B to chromatin which mediate monoubiquitination of
CC       'Lys-120' of histone H2B (H2BK120ub1); UB2A/B-mediated H2B
CC       ubiquitination is proposed to be coupled to transcription. PAF1C
CC       is involved in mRNA 3' end formation probably through association
CC       with cleavage and poly(A) factors. In case of infection by
CC       influenza A strain H3N2, PAF1C associates with viral NS1 protein,
CC       thereby regulating gene transcription. Involved in polyadenylation
CC       of mRNA precursors. Connects PAF1C to Wnt signaling.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15632063, ECO:0000269|PubMed:15791002,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19345177, ECO:0000269|PubMed:19952111,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:20178742}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: Component of the PAF1 complex, which consists of CDC73,
CC       PAF1, LEO1, CTR9, RTF1 and WDR61 (PubMed:15632063,
CC       PubMed:19952111, PubMed:20178742). The PAF1 complex interacts with
CC       PHF5A (By similarity). Interacts with TCEA1, SUPT5H and CTNNB1
CC       (PubMed:16630820, PubMed:19952111, PubMed:20178742). Interacts
CC       with SETD5 (By similarity). {ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:Q5XJE5,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:15632063, ECO:0000269|PubMed:16630820,
CC       ECO:0000269|PubMed:19952111, ECO:0000269|PubMed:20178742}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q6P1J9:CDC73; NbExp=15; IntAct=EBI-932432, EBI-930143;
CC       P35222:CTNNB1; NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-932432, EBI-491549;
CC       Q8N7H5:PAF1; NbExp=23; IntAct=EBI-932432, EBI-2607770;
CC       P23193:TCEA1; NbExp=4; IntAct=EBI-932432, EBI-2608271;
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Nucleus {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15791002}.
CC   -!- ALTERNATIVE PRODUCTS:
CC       Event=Alternative splicing; Named isoforms=2;
CC       Name=1;
CC         IsoId=Q8WVC0-1; Sequence=Displayed;
CC       Name=2;
CC         IsoId=Q8WVC0-2; Sequence=VSP_020051;
CC         Note=No experimental confirmation available. Ref.2 (BAB71006)
CC         sequence differs from that shown due to a frameshift in position
CC         471. {ECO:0000305};
CC   -!- TISSUE SPECIFICITY: Highly expressed in skeletal muscle and heart.
CC       Weakly expressed in placenta and liver.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:15791002}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the LEO1 family. {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: G-protein coupled receptor for glutamate. Ligand binding
CC       causes a conformation change that triggers signaling via guanine
CC       nucleotide-binding proteins (G proteins) and modulates the
CC       activity of down-stream effectors. Signaling activates a
CC       phosphatidylinositol-calcium second messenger system and generates
CC       a calcium-activated chloride current. Plays an important role in
CC       the regulation of synaptic plasticity and the modulation of the
CC       neural network activity (By similarity). {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- SUBUNIT: The PPXXF motif binds HOMER1, HOMER2 and HOMER3.
CC       Interacts with RYR1, RYR2, ITPR1, SHANK1 and SHANK3 (By
CC       similarity). Interacts with SIAH1 and GRASP. Interacts with NCDN.
CC       Interacts with NECAB2 (By similarity). {ECO:0000250,
CC       ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P31424, ECO:0000250|UniProtKB:P41594}.
CC   -!- INTERACTION:
CC       Q9Z214:Homer1 (xeno); NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-8795045, EBI-2338940;
CC       Q9Z214-1:Homer1 (xeno); NbExp=3; IntAct=EBI-8795045, EBI-4410552;
CC       Q9Z214-3:Homer1 (xeno); NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-8795045, EBI-2339003;
CC       Q13526:PIN1 (xeno); NbExp=2; IntAct=EBI-8795045, EBI-714158;

CC       membrane protein {ECO:0000250}.

CC       spleen. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:14674884}.
CC   -!- DISEASE: Combined oxidative phosphorylation deficiency 28
CC       (COXPD28) [MIM:616794]: An autosomal recessive mitochondrial
CC       disorder characterized by decreased activities of respiratory
CC       chain enzymes, and variable clinical manifestations. Clinical
CC       features include episodic metabolic decompensation beginning in
CC       infancy, mild muscle weakness, cardiorespiratory insufficiency,
CC       developmental delay, or even death. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:26522469}.
CC       Note=The disease is caused by mutations affecting the gene
CC       represented in this entry.
